<pr_description>
mv: Behavior different from gnu when moving directory symbolic links (nixos-rebuild switch fails)
Hey, (as we were talking on #help on Discord) I think we might actually have a bug here.  (edit: well, we do - it was reproduced)


When I try rebuilding switch my NixOS system, even using the gnu ln (due to #6350) I still stumble on that mv error making the switch fail. See: https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/62092e522557eebe13946f5fa5a4b16b53faa6e0/new-new-log-file

This ```mv: cannot move '/run/wrappers/bin-tmp' to '/run/wrappers/bin': Directory not empty``` error does not happens when using the gnu mv. Hardcoding the script to use gnu mv makes the nixos-rebuild switch successful! See: https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/324f1bc4d3180e8b6485a765c1b8c21360972c99/log-file-but-fixed-maybe


I once again made those scripts print the stat (and ls) of the stuff it’s messing with, before and after the mv command (uutils only has the before, because mv fails).
  - Uutils: https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/62092e522557eebe13946f5fa5a4b16b53faa6e0/log-stat-mv
  - Gnu: https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/324f1bc4d3180e8b6485a765c1b8c21360972c99/log-stat-mv-gnu


If it helps with the troubleshooting, here’s the complete script in which the problematic mv is located: https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/62092e522557eebe13946f5fa5a4b16b53faa6e0/suid-strt-troubleshoot#L168

Additionally, just like on the 6350 case, both /run/… paths are symbolic links to directories. And just like on that case, this problem does not happens at boot (when /run/wrappers/bin probably doesn’t exist yet) - it only happens when switching on a booted system (when that path does exist).



</pr_description>

    63	/// Options contains all the possible behaviors and flags for mv.
    64	///
    65	/// All options are public so that the options can be programmatically
    66	/// constructed by other crates, such as nushell. That means that this struct is
    67	/// part of our public API. It should therefore not be changed without good reason.
    68	///
    69	/// The fields are documented with the arguments that determine their value.
    70	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq)]
    71	pub struct Options {
    72	    /// specifies overwrite behavior
    73	    /// '-n' '--no-clobber'
    74	    /// '-i' '--interactive'
    75	    /// '-f' '--force'
    76	    pub overwrite: OverwriteMode,
    77	
    78	    /// `--backup[=CONTROL]`, `-b`
    79	    pub backup: BackupMode,
    80	
    81	    /// '-S' --suffix' backup suffix
    82	    pub suffix: String,
    83	
    84	    /// Available update mode "--update-mode=all|none|older"
    85	    pub update: UpdateMode,
    86	
    87	    /// Specifies target directory
    88	    /// '-t, --target-directory=DIRECTORY'
    89	    pub target_dir: Option<OsString>,
    90	
    91	    /// Treat destination as a normal file
    92	    /// '-T, --no-target-directory
    93	    pub no_target_dir: bool,
    94	
    95	    /// '-v, --verbose'
    96	    pub verbose: bool,
    97	
    98	    /// '--strip-trailing-slashes'
    99	    pub strip_slashes: bool,
   100	
   101	    /// '-g, --progress'
   102	    pub progress_bar: bool,
   103	
   104	    /// `--debug`
   105	    pub debug: bool,
   106	
   107	    /// `-Z, --context`
   108	    pub context: Option<String>,
   109	}
   110	
   111	impl Default for Options {
   112	    fn default() -> Self {
   113	        Self {
   114	            overwrite: OverwriteMode::default(),
   115	            backup: BackupMode::default(),
   116	            suffix: backup_control::DEFAULT_BACKUP_SUFFIX.to_owned(),
   117	            update: UpdateMode::default(),
   118	            target_dir: None,
   119	            no_target_dir: false,
   120	            verbose: false,
   121	            strip_slashes: false,
   122	            progress_bar: false,
   123	            debug: false,
   124	            context: None,
   125	        }
   126	    }
   127	}
   128	
   129	/// specifies behavior of the overwrite flag
   130	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Default)]
   131	pub enum OverwriteMode {
   132	    /// '-n' '--no-clobber'   do not overwrite
   133	    NoClobber,
   134	    /// '-i' '--interactive'  prompt before overwrite
   135	    Interactive,
   136	    ///'-f' '--force'         overwrite without prompt
   137	    #[default]
   138	    Force,
   139	}
   140	
   141	static OPT_FORCE: &str = "force";
   142	static OPT_INTERACTIVE: &str = "interactive";
   143	static OPT_NO_CLOBBER: &str = "no-clobber";
   144	static OPT_STRIP_TRAILING_SLASHES: &str = "strip-trailing-slashes";
   145	static OPT_TARGET_DIRECTORY: &str = "target-directory";
   146	static OPT_NO_TARGET_DIRECTORY: &str = "no-target-directory";
   147	static OPT_VERBOSE: &str = "verbose";
   148	static OPT_PROGRESS: &str = "progress";
   149	static ARG_FILES: &str = "files";
   150	static OPT_DEBUG: &str = "debug";
   151	static OPT_CONTEXT: &str = "context";
   152	static OPT_SELINUX: &str = "selinux";
   153	
   154	#[uucore::main]
   155	pub fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
   156	    let matches = uu_app().get_matches_from_localized(args);
   157	
   158	    let files: Vec<OsString> = matches
   159	        .get_many::<OsString>(ARG_FILES)
   160	        .unwrap_or_default()
   161	        .cloned()
   162	        .collect();
   163	
   164	    if files.len() == 1 && !matches.contains_id(OPT_TARGET_DIRECTORY) {
   165	        let err = uu_app().error(
   166	            ErrorKind::TooFewValues,
   167	            translate!("mv-error-insufficient-arguments", "arg_files" => ARG_FILES),
   168	        );
   169	        uucore::clap_localization::handle_clap_error_with_exit_code(err, uucore::util_name(), 1);
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    let overwrite_mode = determine_overwrite_mode(&matches);
   173	    let backup_mode = backup_control::determine_backup_mode(&matches)?;
   174	    let update_mode = update_control::determine_update_mode(&matches);
   175	
   176	    if backup_mode != BackupMode::None
   177	        && (overwrite_mode == OverwriteMode::NoClobber
   178	            || update_mode == UpdateMode::None
   179	            || update_mode == UpdateMode::NoneFail)
   180	    {
   181	        return Err(UUsageError::new(
   182	            1,
   183	            translate!("mv-error-backup-with-no-clobber"),
   184	        ));
   185	    }
   186	
   187	    let backup_suffix = backup_control::determine_backup_suffix(&matches);
   188	
   189	    let target_dir = matches
   190	        .get_one::<OsString>(OPT_TARGET_DIRECTORY)
   191	        .map(OsString::from);
   192	
   193	    if let Some(ref maybe_dir) = target_dir {
   194	        if !Path::new(&maybe_dir).is_dir() {
   195	            return Err(MvError::TargetNotADirectory(maybe_dir.quote().to_string()).into());
   196	        }
   197	    }
   198	
   199	    // Handle -Z and --context options
   200	    // If -Z is used, use the default context (empty string)
   201	    // If --context=value is used, use that specific value
   202	    let context = if matches.get_flag(OPT_SELINUX) {
   203	        Some(String::new())
   204	    } else {
   205	        matches.get_one::<String>(OPT_CONTEXT).cloned()
   206	    };
   207	
   208	    let opts = Options {
   209	        overwrite: overwrite_mode,
   210	        backup: backup_mode,
   211	        suffix: backup_suffix,
   212	        update: update_mode,
   213	        target_dir,
   214	        no_target_dir: matches.get_flag(OPT_NO_TARGET_DIRECTORY),
   215	        verbose: matches.get_flag(OPT_VERBOSE) || matches.get_flag(OPT_DEBUG),
   216	        strip_slashes: matches.get_flag(OPT_STRIP_TRAILING_SLASHES),
   217	        progress_bar: matches.get_flag(OPT_PROGRESS),
   218	        debug: matches.get_flag(OPT_DEBUG),
   219	        context,
   220	    };
   221	
   222	    mv(&files[..], &opts)
   223	}

   225	pub fn uu_app() -> Command {
   226	    Command::new(uucore::util_name())
   227	        .version(uucore::crate_version!())
   228	        .about(translate!("mv-about"))
   229	        .help_template(uucore::localized_help_template(uucore::util_name()))
   230	        .override_usage(format_usage(&translate!("mv-usage")))
   231	        .after_help(format!(
   232	            "{}\n\n{}",
   233	            translate!("mv-after-help"),
   234	            backup_control::BACKUP_CONTROL_LONG_HELP
   235	        ))
   236	        .infer_long_args(true)
   237	        .arg(
   238	            Arg::new(OPT_FORCE)
   239	                .short('f')

   241	                .help(translate!("mv-help-force"))
   242	                .overrides_with_all([OPT_INTERACTIVE, OPT_NO_CLOBBER])
   243	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   244	        )
   245	        .arg(
   246	            Arg::new(OPT_INTERACTIVE)
   247	                .short('i')

   249	                .help(translate!("mv-help-interactive"))
   250	                .overrides_with_all([OPT_FORCE, OPT_NO_CLOBBER])

   252	        )
   253	        .arg(
   254	            Arg::new(OPT_NO_CLOBBER)
   255	                .short('n')
   256	                .long(OPT_NO_CLOBBER)
   257	                .help(translate!("mv-help-no-clobber"))
   258	                .overrides_with_all([OPT_FORCE, OPT_INTERACTIVE])

   261	        .arg(

   269	        .arg(backup_control::arguments::suffix())

   272	        .arg(

   275	                .long(OPT_TARGET_DIRECTORY)
   276	                .help(translate!("mv-help-target-directory"))
   277	                .value_name("DIRECTORY")
   278	                .value_hint(clap::ValueHint::DirPath)
   279	                .conflicts_with(OPT_NO_TARGET_DIRECTORY)
   280	                .value_parser(ValueParser::os_string()),
   281	        )
   282	        .arg(
   283	            Arg::new(OPT_NO_TARGET_DIRECTORY)
   284	                .short('T')
   285	                .long(OPT_NO_TARGET_DIRECTORY)
   286	                .help(translate!("mv-help-no-target-directory"))
   287	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   288	        )
   289	        .arg(
   290	            Arg::new(OPT_VERBOSE)
   291	                .short('v')
   292	                .long(OPT_VERBOSE)
   293	                .help(translate!("mv-help-verbose"))
   294	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   295	        )
   296	        .arg(
   297	            Arg::new(OPT_PROGRESS)
   298	                .short('g')
   299	                .long(OPT_PROGRESS)
   300	                .help(translate!("mv-help-progress"))
   301	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   302	        )
   303	        .arg(
   304	            Arg::new(OPT_SELINUX)
   305	                .short('Z')
   306	                .help(translate!("mv-help-selinux"))
   307	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   308	        )
   309	        .arg(
   310	            Arg::new(OPT_CONTEXT)
   311	                .long(OPT_CONTEXT)
   312	                .value_name("CTX")
   313	                .value_parser(clap::value_parser!(String))
   314	                .help(translate!("mv-help-context"))
   315	                .num_args(0..=1)
   316	                .require_equals(true)
   317	                .default_missing_value(""),

   322	                .num_args(1..)
   323	                .required(true)
   324	                .value_parser(ValueParser::os_string())

   326	        )

   332	        )
   333	}
   334	
   335	fn determine_overwrite_mode(matches: &ArgMatches) -> OverwriteMode {
   336	    // This does not exactly match the GNU implementation:
   337	    // The GNU mv defaults to Force, but if more than one of the
   338	    // overwrite options are supplied, only the last takes effect.
   339	    // To default to no-clobber in that situation seems safer:
   340	    //
   341	    if matches.get_flag(OPT_NO_CLOBBER) {
   342	        OverwriteMode::NoClobber
   343	    } else if matches.get_flag(OPT_INTERACTIVE) {
   344	        OverwriteMode::Interactive
   345	    } else {
   346	        OverwriteMode::Force
   347	    }
   348	}
   349	
   350	fn parse_paths(files: &[OsString], opts: &Options) -> Vec<PathBuf> {
   351	    let paths = files.iter().map(Path::new);
   352	
   353	    if opts.strip_slashes {
   354	        paths
   355	            .map(|p| p.components().as_path().to_owned())
   356	            .collect::<Vec<PathBuf>>()
   357	    } else {
   358	        paths.map(|p| p.to_owned()).collect::<Vec<PathBuf>>()
   359	    }
   360	}
   361	
   362	fn handle_two_paths(source: &Path, target: &Path, opts: &Options) -> UResult<()> {
   363	    if opts.backup == BackupMode::Simple && source_is_target_backup(source, target, &opts.suffix) {
   364	        return Err(io::Error::new(
   365	            io::ErrorKind::NotFound,
   366	            translate!("mv-error-backup-might-destroy-source", "target" => target.quote(), "source" => source.quote()),
   367	        )
   368	        .into());
   369	    }
   370	    if source.symlink_metadata().is_err() {
   371	        return Err(if path_ends_with_terminator(source) {
   372	            MvError::CannotStatNotADirectory(source.quote().to_string()).into()
   373	        } else {
   374	            MvError::NoSuchFile(source.quote().to_string()).into()
   375	        });
   376	    }
   377	
   378	    let target_is_dir = target.is_dir();
   379	    let source_is_dir = source.is_dir();
   380	
   381	    if path_ends_with_terminator(target)
   382	        && (!target_is_dir && !source_is_dir)
   383	        && !opts.no_target_dir
   384	        && opts.update != UpdateMode::IfOlder
   385	    {
   386	        return Err(MvError::FailedToAccessNotADirectory(target.quote().to_string()).into());
   387	    }
   388	
   389	    assert_not_same_file(source, target, target_is_dir, opts)?;
   390	
   391	    if target_is_dir {
   392	        if opts.no_target_dir {
   393	            if source.is_dir() {
   394	                #[cfg(unix)]
   395	                let (mut hardlink_tracker, hardlink_scanner) = create_hardlink_context();
   396	                #[cfg(unix)]
   397	                let hardlink_params = (Some(&mut hardlink_tracker), Some(&hardlink_scanner));
   398	                #[cfg(not(unix))]
   399	                let hardlink_params = (None, None);
   400	
   401	                rename(
   402	                    source,
   403	                    target,
   404	                    opts,
   405	                    None,
   406	                    hardlink_params.0,
   407	                    hardlink_params.1,
   408	                )
   409	                .map_err_context(|| {
   410	                    translate!("mv-error-cannot-move", "source" => source.quote(), "target" => target.quote())
   411	                })
   412	            } else {
   413	                Err(MvError::DirectoryToNonDirectory(target.quote().to_string()).into())
   414	            }
   415	        } else {
   416	            move_files_into_dir(&[source.to_path_buf()], target, opts)
   417	        }
   418	    } else if target.exists() && source.is_dir() {
   419	        match opts.overwrite {
   420	            OverwriteMode::NoClobber => return Ok(()),
   421	            OverwriteMode::Interactive => {
   422	                if !prompt_yes!(
   423	                    "{}",
   424	                    translate!("mv-prompt-overwrite", "target" => target.quote())
   425	                ) {
   426	                    return Err(io::Error::other("").into());
   427	                }
   428	            }
   429	            OverwriteMode::Force => {}
   430	        }
   431	        Err(MvError::NonDirectoryToDirectory(
   432	            source.quote().to_string(),
   433	            target.quote().to_string(),
   434	        )
   435	        .into())
   436	    } else {
   437	        #[cfg(unix)]
   438	        let (mut hardlink_tracker, hardlink_scanner) = create_hardlink_context();
   439	        #[cfg(unix)]
   440	        let hardlink_params = (Some(&mut hardlink_tracker), Some(&hardlink_scanner));
   441	        #[cfg(not(unix))]
   442	        let hardlink_params = (None, None);
   443	
   444	        rename(
   445	            source,
   446	            target,
   447	            opts,
   448	            None,
   449	            hardlink_params.0,
   450	            hardlink_params.1,
   451	        )
   452	        .map_err(|e| USimpleError::new(1, format!("{e}")))
   453	    }
   454	}
   455	
   456	fn assert_not_same_file(
   457	    source: &Path,
   458	    target: &Path,
   459	    target_is_dir: bool,
   460	    opts: &Options,
   461	) -> UResult<()> {
   462	    // we'll compare canonicalized_source and canonicalized_target for same file detection
   463	    let canonicalized_source = match canonicalize(
   464	        absolute(source)?,
   465	        MissingHandling::Normal,
   466	        ResolveMode::Logical,
   467	    ) {
   468	        Ok(source) if source.exists() => source,
   469	        _ => absolute(source)?, // file or symlink target doesn't exist but its absolute path is still used for comparison
   470	    };
   471	
   472	    // special case if the target exists, is a directory, and the `-T` flag wasn't used
   473	    let target_is_dir = target_is_dir && !opts.no_target_dir;
   474	    let canonicalized_target = if target_is_dir {
   475	        // `mv source_file target_dir` => target_dir/source_file

   803	
   804	/// A wrapper around `fs::rename`, so that if it fails, we try falling back on
   805	/// copying and removing.
   806	fn rename_with_fallback(
   807	    from: &Path,
   808	    to: &Path,
   809	    multi_progress: Option<&MultiProgress>,
   810	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_tracker: Option<&mut HardlinkTracker>,
   811	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_scanner: Option<&HardlinkGroupScanner>,
   812	    #[cfg(not(unix))] _hardlink_tracker: Option<()>,
   813	    #[cfg(not(unix))] _hardlink_scanner: Option<()>,
   814	) -> io::Result<()> {
   815	    fs::rename(from, to).or_else(|err| {
   816	        #[cfg(windows)]
   817	        const EXDEV: i32 = windows_sys::Win32::Foundation::ERROR_NOT_SAME_DEVICE as _;
   818	        #[cfg(unix)]
   819	        const EXDEV: i32 = libc::EXDEV as _;
   820	
   821	        // We will only copy if:
   822	        // 1. Files are on different devices (EXDEV error)
   823	        // 2. On Windows, if the target file exists and source file is opened by another process
   824	        //    (MoveFileExW fails with "Access Denied" even if the source file has FILE_SHARE_DELETE permission)
   825	        let should_fallback =
   826	            matches!(err.raw_os_error(), Some(EXDEV)) || (from.is_file() && can_delete_file(from));
   827	        if !should_fallback {
   828	            return Err(err);
   829	        }
   830	        // Get metadata without following symlinks
   831	        let metadata = from.symlink_metadata()?;
   832	        let file_type = metadata.file_type();
   833	        if file_type.is_symlink() {
   834	            rename_symlink_fallback(from, to)
   835	        } else if file_type.is_dir() {
   836	            #[cfg(unix)]
   837	            {
   838	                with_optional_hardlink_context(
   839	                    hardlink_tracker,
   840	                    hardlink_scanner,
   841	                    |tracker, scanner| {
   842	                        rename_dir_fallback(from, to, multi_progress, Some(tracker), Some(scanner))
   843	                    },
   844	                )
   845	            }
   846	            #[cfg(not(unix))]
   847	            {
   848	                rename_dir_fallback(from, to, multi_progress)
   849	            }
   850	        } else if is_fifo(file_type) {
   851	            rename_fifo_fallback(from, to)
   852	        } else {
   853	            #[cfg(unix)]
   854	            {
   855	                with_optional_hardlink_context(
   856	                    hardlink_tracker,
   857	                    hardlink_scanner,
   858	                    |tracker, scanner| rename_file_fallback(from, to, Some(tracker), Some(scanner)),
   859	                )
   860	            }
   861	            #[cfg(not(unix))]
   862	            {
   863	                rename_file_fallback(from, to)
   864	            }
   865	        }
   866	    })
   867	}
   868	
   869	/// Replace the destination with a new pipe with the same name as the source.
   870	#[cfg(unix)]
   871	fn rename_fifo_fallback(from: &Path, to: &Path) -> io::Result<()> {
   872	    if to.try_exists()? {
   873	        fs::remove_file(to)?;
   874	    }
   875	    make_fifo(to).and_then(|_| fs::remove_file(from))
   876	}
   877	
   878	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   879	fn rename_fifo_fallback(_from: &Path, _to: &Path) -> io::Result<()> {
   880	    Ok(())
   881	}
   882	
   883	/// Move the given symlink to the given destination. On Windows, dangling
   884	/// symlinks return an error.
   885	#[cfg(unix)]
   886	fn rename_symlink_fallback(from: &Path, to: &Path) -> io::Result<()> {
   887	    let path_symlink_points_to = fs::read_link(from)?;
   888	    unix::fs::symlink(path_symlink_points_to, to).and_then(|_| fs::remove_file(from))
   889	}
   890	
   891	#[cfg(windows)]
   892	fn rename_symlink_fallback(from: &Path, to: &Path) -> io::Result<()> {
   893	    let path_symlink_points_to = fs::read_link(from)?;
   894	    if path_symlink_points_to.exists() {
   895	        if path_symlink_points_to.is_dir() {
   896	            windows::fs::symlink_dir(&path_symlink_points_to, to)?;
   897	        } else {
   898	            windows::fs::symlink_file(&path_symlink_points_to, to)?;
   899	        }
   900	        fs::remove_file(from)
   901	    } else {
   902	        Err(io::Error::new(
   903	            io::ErrorKind::NotFound,
   904	            translate!("mv-error-dangling-symlink"),
   905	        ))
   906	    }
   907	}
   908	
   909	#[cfg(not(any(windows, unix)))]
   910	fn rename_symlink_fallback(from: &Path, to: &Path) -> io::Result<()> {
   911	    let path_symlink_points_to = fs::read_link(from)?;
   912	    Err(io::Error::new(
   913	        io::ErrorKind::Other,
   914	        translate!("mv-error-no-symlink-support"),
   915	    ))
   916	}

2026-06-01 04:54:55,362 - INFO - swea-agent-uutils__coreutils-8528 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the issue! Look at lines 750-759:

```rust
    // "to" may no longer exist if it was backed up
    if to.exists() && to.is_dir() {
        // normalize behavior between *nix and windows
        if from.is_dir() {
            if is_empty_dir(to) {
                fs::remove_dir(to)?;
            } else {
                return Err(io::Error::other(translate!("mv-error-directory-not-empty")));
            }
        }
    }
```

The problem is clear: when `to` (the target) is a symbolic link pointing to a directory, `to.is_dir()` returns `true` (because it follows symlinks). But `from.is_dir()` also follows symlinks. The issue described in the PR is about moving a directory symlink where the target is also a symlink to a directory.

The PR says:
- Both `/run/wrappers/bin-tmp` and `/run/wrappers/bin` are symbolic links to directories.
- When `mv /run/wrappers/bin-tmp /run/wrappers/bin` is called, it fails with "Directory not empty".
- GNU `mv` handles this correctly.

The problem is that when `to` is a symlink pointing to a directory:
1. `to.exists() && to.is_dir()` is true
2. `from.is_dir()` is also true (since from is also a symlink to a directory)
3. Then it checks if `to` is empty - but `to` is a symlink pointing to a directory, and the directory it points to is non-empty
4. So it returns "Directory not empty"

But the correct behavior should be to replace the symlink itself, not look at what the symlink points to. The issue is that `std::fs::rename` would actually succeed here (it renames the symlink itself, not following it), but the pre-check in lines 750-759 blocks it.

Let me verify by checking the actual `rename` behavior: `fs::rename` on Unix doesn't follow symlinks for the source, so it should just work. The pre-check is wrong.

Let me also look at what happens when the destination exists and is a directory (not a symlink, but an actual directory). In that case, the current behavior (checking if it's empty) makes sense - but only when the source is also a directory (not a symlink to a directory). But wait, even then: if source is a directory symlink and destination is a real directory, we probably still want the rename to succeed (it would fail with "Directory not empty" from the kernel if the directory is non-empty).

Let me think more carefully:

1. Case: `mv /run/wrappers/bin-tmp /run/wrappers/bin` where both are symlinks to directories.
   - `from` is symlink -> directory A
   - `to` is symlink -> directory B
   - The correct behavior (GNU): rename the symlink itself, i.e., make `bin` point to directory A instead of B, and remove `bin-tmp`.
   - Current behavior: the pre-check sees `to.is_dir()` is true, `from.is_dir()` is true, checks if the directory B is empty, it's not, so fails.

2. Case: `mv source_dir target_symlink_to_dir` where source is a real directory
   - `from` is real dir
   - `to` is symlink to dir
   - What should happen? The rename syscall would try to rename the directory to the symlink path. But `rename("dir", "symlink")` where symlink points to a directory... actually `rename` would replace the symlink with the directory. Let me double-check: `man 2 rename` says if newpath is a symbolic link, it is not followed.

So the fix should be: when `to` is a symlink, we should not do the pre-check (or we should treat it differently). The pre-check only applies when `to` is an actual directory (not a symlink to one).

  1096	    if to.is_symlink() {
  1097	        fs::remove_file(to).map_err(|err| {

  1099	            io::Error::new(err.kind(), inter_device_msg)
  1100	        })?;
  1101	    } else if to.exists() {
  1102	        // For non-symlinks, just remove the file without special error handling
  1103	        fs::remove_file(to)?;
  1104	    }
  1105

  1107	    #[cfg(unix)]
  1108	    {
  1109	        if let (Some(tracker), Some(scanner)) = (hardlink_tracker, hardlink_scanner) {
  1110	            use crate::hardlink::HardlinkOptions;
  1111	            let hardlink_options = HardlinkOptions::default();

  1113	                tracker.check_hardlink(from, to, scanner, &hardlink_options)?
  1114	            {

  1116	                fs::hard_link(&existing_target, to)?;
  1117	                fs::remove_file(from)?;
  1118	                return Ok(());
  1119	            }

Now I have a clear picture. The fix should be in the `rename` function at lines 750-759. We need to check whether `to` is a symlink, and if so, skip the directory-emptiness check because `fs::rename` handles symlinks correctly (it doesn't follow them).

Also, we should check if `from` is a symlink as well - if `from` is a symlink to a directory and `to` is an actual directory, the `rename` syscall would still work (it renames the symlink). But wait, `from.is_dir()` would return true for a symlink to a directory. Let's think about all the cases:

Actually, let me re-read the PR description more carefully:

> Additionally, just like on the 6350 case, both /run/… paths are symbolic links to directories. And just like on that case, this problem does not happens at boot (when /run/wrappers/bin probably doesn't exist yet) - it only happens when switching on a booted system (when that path does exist).

So both `from` and `to` are symlinks to directories. The correct behavior is to rename the symlink, not to check the contents of the directory it points to.

The fix should be to not do the directory check when `to` is a symlink. Let me also consider what happens if `from` is a real directory and `to` is a symlink - the `rename` syscall should handle that correctly too.

But there's also another subtlety: what if `from` is a symlink to a directory and `to` is a real directory? The `rename` syscall would fail with "Directory not empty" (from the kernel) if the target directory is non-empty. But our current code would also catch that. So the only case we need to fix is when `to` is a symlink.

Wait, actually let me think again. The `rename` syscall for directories: if `to` exists and is an empty directory, rename succeeds (the target directory is replaced). If `to` exists and is a non-empty directory, rename fails with ENOTEMPTY. But if `to` is a symlink to a directory, the kernel's `rename` doesn't follow the symlink - it just replaces the symlink itself. So `rename("src_symlink", "dst_symlink")` should always work (assuming permissions are OK).

So the fix is: in the pre-check at lines 750-759, we should skip the check when `to` is a symlink. The kernel will handle it correctly.

Let me write a script to reproduce this:

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_mv_symlink.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
set -e

# Create a temporary test directory
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"

# Create two directories
mkdir -p dirA
mkdir -p dirB

# Put something in dirB so it's non-empty
touch dirB/somefile

# Create symlinks to each
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB

echo "=== Setup ==="
ls -la
echo ""
echo "linkA -> $(readlink linkA)"
echo "linkB -> $(readlink linkB)"
echo ""

# Now try to mv linkA to linkB (this should work like GNU mv)
echo "=== Running: mv linkA linkB ==="
# Use the uutils mv from the build
/target/debug/coreutils mv linkA linkB
echo "Exit code: $?"

echo ""
echo "=== Result ==="
ls -la
echo ""
if [ -L linkB ]; then
    echo "linkB -> $(readlink linkB)"
else
    echo "linkB is not a symlink"
fi
if [ -e linkA ]; then
    echo "linkA still exists"
else
    echo "linkA was removed"
fi

rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
EOF

Let me re-read the code more carefully. Looking at line 750-759:

```rust
// "to" may no longer exist if it was backed up
if to.exists() && to.is_dir() {
    // normalize behavior between *nix and windows
    if from.is_dir() {
        if is_empty_dir(to) {
            fs::remove_dir(to)?;
        } else {
            return Err(io::Error::other(translate!("mv-error-directory-not-empty")));
        }
    }
}
```

Wait, the condition is `to.exists() && to.is_dir()`. For a symlink to a directory, `to.is_dir()` returns true. But `to.exists()` also returns true for a symlink to an existing directory.

1. `to.exists()` - true for symlink to existing dir
2. `to.is_dir()` - true for symlink to dir
3. `from.is_dir()` - true for symlink to dir (since `Path::is_dir()` follows symlinks)
4. `is_empty_dir(to)` - this checks if the directory pointed to by the symlink is empty

```rust
if target_is_dir {
    if opts.no_target_dir {
        if source.is_dir() {
            // ... rename(...)
        }
    } else {
        move_files_into_dir(...)
    }
}
```

cat > /tmp/test_fix.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
set -e

TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"

mkdir -p dirA
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB

echo "=== Test 1: mv -T linkA linkB (symlink to symlink) ==="
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T linkA linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo ""
ls -la
echo "linkB -> $(readlink linkB)"
echo ""

# Clean up
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 2: source is symlink, dest is real directory
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA

echo "=== Test 2: mv -T linkA dirB (symlink to real dir, non-empty) ==="
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T linkA dirB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo ""
ls -la
echo ""

rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 3: source is real directory, dest is symlink to non-empty dir
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirB linkB

echo "=== Test 3: mv -T dirA linkB (real dir to symlink to non-empty dir) ==="
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T dirA linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo ""
ls -la
echo ""

rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 4: source is real directory, dest is real non-empty directory
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile

echo "=== Test 4: mv -T dirA dirB (real dir to real non-empty dir) ==="
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T dirA dirB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo ""
ls -la
echo ""

rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

echo "All tests completed."
EOF

Good, the non-`-T` case already works correctly (it moves into the directory).

Now let me also look at the `handle_two_paths` function more closely to see if there's another place where symlink handling could be improved. In particular, look at lines 391-414:

```rust
if target_is_dir {
    if opts.no_target_dir {
        if source.is_dir() {
            // rename...
        } else {
            Err(MvError::DirectoryToNonDirectory(...))
        }
    } else {
        move_files_into_dir(...)
    }
} else if target.exists() && source.is_dir() {
    // ...
    Err(MvError::NonDirectoryToDirectory(...))
}
```

The issue is that `target_is_dir` and `source.is_dir()` follow symlinks. When `-T` is used and the target is a symlink to a directory, we want to replace the symlink, not treat it as a directory. But the current code treats it as a directory and then goes into the rename path, which would work with my fix.

But there's another case: what if `-T` is used, target is a symlink to a directory, but source is NOT a directory (e.g., a regular file)? Then:
- `target_is_dir` = true (symlink to dir)
- `source.is_dir()` = false
- Goes to `Err(MvError::DirectoryToNonDirectory(...))` 

But GNU would actually succeed: it would rename the regular file to the symlink path, replacing the symlink. Let me test:

Yes, this is another bug. But the PR description focuses on the case where both are symlinks to directories. Let me check if the PR description mentions this other case too... It says "both /run/… paths are symbolic links to directories." So it's specifically the case where source and target are both symlinks to directories.

But I should also check: in the NixOS script, does it use `-T`? Let me look at the referenced script. The PR links to https://github.com/LuNeder/nixos-config/blob/62092e522557eebe13946f5fa5a4b16b53faa6e0/suid-strt-troubleshoot#L168

I can't access that, but based on the PR description, the key issue is that when both paths are symlinks to directories, mv should replace the symlink, not check the directory contents.

Now let me think about what the complete fix should be. My current fix handles the `rename()` function. But there's also the issue in `handle_two_paths` where `target_is_dir` is used to determine the code path. 

Actually, let me look at this more carefully. In the `handle_two_paths` function:

```rust
let target_is_dir = target.is_dir();  // follows symlinks!
let source_is_dir = source.is_dir();   // follows symlinks!

if target_is_dir {
    if opts.no_target_dir {
        if source.is_dir() {
            // rename...
        } else {
            Err(MvError::DirectoryToNonDirectory(...))
        }
    } else {
        move_files_into_dir(...)
    }
}
```

When both are symlinks to directories and `-T` is used:
- `target_is_dir` = true
- `source.is_dir()` = true
- Goes to `rename()`, which with my fix now works correctly.

But when source is a regular file, target is a symlink to a directory, and `-T` is used:
- `target_is_dir` = true
- `source.is_dir()` = false
- Goes to `Err(MvError::DirectoryToNonDirectory(...))` ← wrong!

The fix for that would be: when `-T` is used, we should check `target.symlink_metadata()` to see if it's a symlink, and if so, treat it as a non-directory.

But wait, let me re-read the PR description again. It says:

> This mv: cannot move '/run/wrappers/bin-tmp' to '/run/wrappers/bin': Directory not empty error does not happens when using the gnu mv.

The error message "Directory not empty" matches our `translate!("mv-error-directory-not-empty")` which is in the `rename()` function. So the main issue is definitely in `rename()`.

But let me also check if there's a possibility that the NixOS script uses `-T` or not. The error message "cannot move '...' to '...': Directory not empty" is from `.map_err_context(|| translate!("mv-error-cannot-move", ...))` at line 409-411. So it goes through the `rename()` function which is called when `-T` is used (or when the target doesn't exist/is a file).

Actually, looking more carefully at the code flow:
1. If target is a directory (including symlink to dir) and NO `-T`: `move_files_into_dir` → would move source INTO the target directory. This wouldn't produce the "Directory not empty" error.
2. If target is a directory and `-T` is used: goes to `rename()`, which could produce the error.
3. If target does NOT exist or is a file (not dir): goes to `rename()` too.

So the error "Directory not empty" would only happen when either:
- `-T` is used and both source and target are directories (or symlinks to directories)
- OR target doesn't exist/is a file, but the pre-check at line 750-759 triggers

But case 3 wouldn't happen because if target doesn't exist, `to.exists()` is false. If target is a file, `to.is_dir()` is false. So the pre-check only triggers when target exists and is a directory.

So the only way to hit this error is when `-T` is used and both paths point to directories (or symlinks to directories). My fix addresses this.

Now, I should also consider whether the `handle_two_paths` function needs to be fixed for the case where `-T` is used and the target is a symlink. Let me check what happens with the PR's main scenario: source is symlink to dir, target is symlink to dir, with `-T`:

With my fix:
- `target_is_dir` = true
- `source.is_dir()` = true
- Goes to `rename()`, which now succeeds.

That's correct!

But what about: source is a regular file, target is symlink to dir, with `-T`? GNU replaces the symlink. Our code returns `DirectoryToNonDirectory`. This is a separate bug but might be worth fixing too since it's related.

Let me look at whether the PR description or related issues mention this case. The PR says:

> both /run/… paths are symbolic links to directories

So both are symlinks to directories. My fix should handle this. But I should also consider fixing the `handle_two_paths` function to handle the case where target is a symlink and `-T` is used.

Actually, let me look at this from a different angle. The `handle_two_paths` function determines whether to treat the target as a directory or not. The GNU behavior is:
- Without `-T`: if target is a directory (or symlink to one), move source INTO it.
- With `-T`: treat target as a non-directory path (just a name to be overwritten), regardless of what it points to.

So the fix for `handle_two_paths` when `-T` is used should be: if target is a symlink, don't treat it as a directory.

#!/bin/bash
set -e

echo "=========================================="
echo "Test 1: mv -T linkA linkB (both symlinks to dirs)"
echo "=========================================="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T linkA linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo "linkB -> $(readlink linkB)"
[ "$(readlink linkB)" = "dirA" ] && echo "PASS" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
echo ""

echo "=========================================="
echo "Test 2: mv -T regular_file linkB (file to symlink-to-dir)"
echo "=========================================="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirB linkB
echo "hello" > regular_file
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T regular_file linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
[ -f linkB ] && [ ! -L linkB ] && echo "PASS" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
echo ""

echo "=========================================="
echo "Test 3: mv -T dirA linkB (real dir to symlink-to-dir)"
echo "=========================================="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirB linkB
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T dirA linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
[ -d linkB ] && [ ! -L linkB ] && echo "PASS" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
echo ""

echo "=========================================="
echo "Test 4: mv -T dirA dirB (real dir to real non-empty dir)"
echo "=========================================="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv -T dirA dirB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
echo "Should have failed with 'Directory not empty'"
[ -d dirA ] && [ -d dirB ] && echo "PASS (both still exist)" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
echo ""

echo "=========================================="
echo "Test 5: mv linkA linkB (no -T, both symlinks to dirs)"
echo "=========================================="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB
"/testbed/target/debug/coreutils" mv linkA linkB 2>&1 || echo "Exit code: $?"
[ -L "dirB/linkA" ] && echo "PASS (linkA moved into dirB)" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"
echo ""

echo "=========================================="
echo "All tests completed."
EOF

- `source_is_dir` = `source.is_dir()` = `true` (symlink to dir)
- Since `target_is_dir` is false, we go to `else if target.exists() && source.is_dir()`:

  - `source.is_dir()` = true
  - Returns `NonDirectoryToDirectory` error

   558	/// file or directory, then 'source' will be renamed to 'target'.
   559	pub fn mv(files: &[OsString], opts: &Options) -> UResult<()> {
   560	    let paths = parse_paths(files, opts);
   561	
   562	    if let Some(ref name) = opts.target_dir {
   563	        return move_files_into_dir(&paths, &PathBuf::from(name), opts);
   564	    }
   565	
   566	    match paths.len() {
   567	        2 => handle_two_paths(&paths[0], &paths[1], opts),
   568	        _ => handle_multiple_paths(&paths, opts),
   569	    }
   570	}
   571	
   572	#[allow(clippy::cognitive_complexity)]
   573	fn move_files_into_dir(files: &[PathBuf], target_dir: &Path, options: &Options) -> UResult<()> {
   574	    // remember the moved destinations for further usage
   575	    let mut moved_destinations: HashSet<PathBuf> = HashSet::with_capacity(files.len());
   576	    // Create hardlink tracking context
   577	    #[cfg(unix)]
   578	    let (mut hardlink_tracker, hardlink_scanner) = {
   579	        let (tracker, mut scanner) = create_hardlink_context();
   580	
   581	        // Use hardlink options
   582	        let hardlink_options = HardlinkOptions {
   583	            verbose: options.verbose || options.debug,
   584	        };
   585	
   586	        // Pre-scan files if needed
   587	        if let Err(e) = scanner.scan_files(files, &hardlink_options) {
   588	            if hardlink_options.verbose {
   589	                eprintln!("mv: warning: failed to scan files for hardlinks: {e}");
   590	                eprintln!("mv: continuing without hardlink preservation");
   591	            } else {
   592	                // Show warning in non-verbose mode for serious errors
   593	                eprintln!(
   594	                    "mv: warning: hardlink scanning failed, continuing without hardlink preservation"
   595	                );
   596	            }
   597	            // Continue without hardlink tracking on scan failure
   598	            // This provides graceful degradation rather than failing completely
   599	        }
   600	
   601	        (tracker, scanner)
   602	    };
   603	
   604	    if !target_dir.is_dir() {
   605	        return Err(MvError::NotADirectory(target_dir.quote().to_string()).into());
   606	    }
   607	
   608	    let multi_progress = options.progress_bar.then(MultiProgress::new);
   609	
   610	    let count_progress = if let Some(ref multi_progress) = multi_progress {
   611	        if files.len() > 1 {
   612	            Some(
   613	                multi_progress.add(
   614	                    ProgressBar::new(files.len().try_into().unwrap()).with_style(
   615	                        ProgressStyle::with_template(&format!(
   616	                            "{} {{msg}} {{wide_bar}} {{pos}}/{{len}}",
   617	                            translate!("mv-progress-moving")
   618	                        ))
   619	                        .unwrap(),
   620	                    ),
   621	                ),
   622	            )
   623	        } else {
   624	            None
   625	        }
   626	    } else {
   627	        None
   628	    };
   629	
   630	    for sourcepath in files {
   631	        if sourcepath.symlink_metadata().is_err() {
   632	            show!(MvError::NoSuchFile(sourcepath.quote().to_string()));
   633	            continue;
   634	        }
   635	
   636	        if let Some(ref pb) = count_progress {
   637	            let msg = format!("{} (scanning hardlinks)", sourcepath.to_string_lossy());
   638	            pb.set_message(msg);
   639	        }
   640	
   641	        let targetpath = match sourcepath.file_name() {
   642	            Some(name) => target_dir.join(name),
   643	            None => {
   644	                show!(MvError::NoSuchFile(sourcepath.quote().to_string()));
   645	                continue;
   646	            }
   647	        };
   648	
   649	        if moved_destinations.contains(&targetpath) && options.backup != BackupMode::Numbered {
   650	            // If the target file was already created in this mv call, do not overwrite
   651	            show!(USimpleError::new(
   652	                1,
   653	                translate!("mv-error-will-not-overwrite-just-created", "target" => targetpath.display(), "source" => sourcepath.display()),
   654	            ));
   655	            continue;
   656	        }
   657	
   658	        // Check if we have mv dir1 dir2 dir2
   659	        // And generate an error if this is the case
   660	        if let Err(e) = assert_not_same_file(sourcepath, target_dir, true, options) {
   661	            show!(e);
   662	            continue;
   663	        }
   664	
   665	        #[cfg(unix)]
   666	        let hardlink_params = (Some(&mut hardlink_tracker), Some(&hardlink_scanner));
   667	        #[cfg(not(unix))]
   668	        let hardlink_params = (None, None);
   669	
   670	        match rename(
   671	            sourcepath,
   672	            &targetpath,
   673	            options,
   674	            multi_progress.as_ref(),
   675	            hardlink_params.0,
   676	            hardlink_params.1,
   677	        ) {
   678	            Err(e) if e.to_string().is_empty() => set_exit_code(1),
   679	            Err(e) => {
   680	                let e = e.map_err_context(|| {
   681	                    translate!("mv-error-cannot-move", "source" => sourcepath.quote(), "target" => targetpath.quote())
   682	                });
   683	                match multi_progress {
   684	                    Some(ref pb) => pb.suspend(|| show!(e)),
   685	                    None => show!(e),
   686	                }
   687	            }
   688	            Ok(()) => (),
   689	        }
   690	        if let Some(ref pb) = count_progress {
   691	            pb.inc(1);
   692	        }

2026-06-01 05:02:55,163 - INFO - swea-agent-uutils__coreutils-8528 - 💭 THOUGHT
So our code says "Directory not empty" but GNU says "cannot overwrite directory with non-directory". This is a different behavior. Let me check what the correct fix should be.

The issue is that in `handle_two_paths`:
- `target_is_dir` = true
- `source.is_dir()` = true (follows symlink)
- Goes to `rename()`, which calls `fs::rename`
- `fs::rename` would actually succeed here? No, wait: `fs::rename` for a symlink to a directory onto a real directory... the kernel's `rename` syscall would replace the directory if it's empty, or fail with ENOTEMPTY if it's not empty.

But GNU says "cannot overwrite directory with non-directory" - it treats the source symlink as a non-directory. So GNU checks: if target is a directory (real, not symlink) and source is a symlink (even to a directory), refuse with "cannot overwrite directory with non-directory".

This is a separate issue from the PR. The PR is about both being symlinks. My fix correctly handles that case.

However, I should also consider the case where source is a symlink to a directory and target is a real directory (non-empty). The current behavior (Directory not empty) is actually also correct in a sense - it matches what the kernel would do. But GNU's behavior is different: it refuses upfront with a different message.

But the PR doesn't mention this case. Let me focus on ensuring the PR's scenario is fixed.

Let me also check if there's a similar issue in the `move_files_into_dir` path. What if the target directory is a symlink to a directory and one of the source files has the same name as an existing file in that directory?

Actually, let me re-read the PR description once more:

> When I try rebuilding switch my NixOS system, even using the gnu ln (due to #6350) I still stumble on that mv error making the switch fail.

> This mv: cannot move '/run/wrappers/bin-tmp' to '/run/wrappers/bin': Directory not empty error

So the error is "Directory not empty" when moving `/run/wrappers/bin-tmp` to `/run/wrappers/bin`. Both are symlinks to directories. The error comes from our pre-check in `rename()`.

My fix handles this. The case where source is a symlink to a directory and target is a real directory is a different issue (and GNU also fails, just with a different message).

Now, let me think about edge cases:

1. What if `from` is a symlink to a non-existent directory? `from.is_dir()` returns false, so the pre-check doesn't trigger. The rename would succeed or fail based on the kernel's behavior.

2. What if `to` is a symlink to a non-existent directory? `to.exists()` returns false (since the target of the symlink doesn't exist). `to.is_dir()` returns false. The pre-check doesn't trigger.

3. What if `to` is a symlink to an empty directory? `to.exists()` returns true, `to.is_dir()` returns true, but `to.is_symlink()` returns true, so the pre-check is skipped. The rename replaces the symlink. This is correct.

4. What if `to` is a symlink to a non-empty directory? Same as #3, pre-check skipped, rename replaces symlink. Correct.

5. What if `to` is a real empty directory? Pre-check runs, directory is empty, removes it, then renames. Correct.

6. What if `to` is a real non-empty directory? Pre-check runs, directory not empty, returns error. Correct.

All edge cases seem to be handled correctly by my fix.

   808	fn is_fifo(_filetype: fs::FileType) -> bool {

   812	/// A wrapper around `fs::rename`, so that if it fails, we try falling back on
   813	/// copying and removing.
   814	fn rename_with_fallback(
   815	    from: &Path,
   816	    to: &Path,
   817	    multi_progress: Option<&MultiProgress>,
   818	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_tracker: Option<&mut HardlinkTracker>,
   819	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_scanner: Option<&HardlinkGroupScanner>,
   820	    #[cfg(not(unix))] _hardlink_tracker: Option<()>,
   821	    #[cfg(not(unix))] _hardlink_scanner: Option<()>,
   822	) -> io::Result<()> {
   823	    fs::rename(from, to).or_else(|err| {
   824	        #[cfg(windows)]
   825	        const EXDEV: i32 = windows_sys::Win32::Foundation::ERROR_NOT_SAME_DEVICE as _;
   826	        #[cfg(unix)]
   827	        const EXDEV: i32 = libc::EXDEV as _;
   828	
   829	        // We will only copy if:
   830	        // 1. Files are on different devices (EXDEV error)
   831	        // 2. On Windows, if the target file exists and source file is opened by another process
   832	        //    (MoveFileExW fails with "Access Denied" even if the source file has FILE_SHARE_DELETE permission)
   833	        let should_fallback =
   834	            matches!(err.raw_os_error(), Some(EXDEV)) || (from.is_file() && can_delete_file(from));
   835	        if !should_fallback {
   836	            return Err(err);
   837	        }
   838	        // Get metadata without following symlinks
   839	        let metadata = from.symlink_metadata()?;
   840	        let file_type = metadata.file_type();
   841	        if file_type.is_symlink() {
   842	            rename_symlink_fallback(from, to)
   843	        } else if file_type.is_dir() {
   844	            #[cfg(unix)]
   845	            {
   846	                with_optional_hardlink_context(
   847	                    hardlink_tracker,
   848	                    hardlink_scanner,
   849	                    |tracker, scanner| {
   850	                        rename_dir_fallback(from, to, multi_progress, Some(tracker), Some(scanner))
   851	                    },
   852	                )
   853	            }
   854	            #[cfg(not(unix))]
   855	            {
   856	                rename_dir_fallback(from, to, multi_progress)
   857	            }
   858	        } else if is_fifo(file_type) {
   859	            rename_fifo_fallback(from, to)
   860	        } else {
   861	            #[cfg(unix)]
   862	            {
   863	                with_optional_hardlink_context(
   864	                    hardlink_tracker,
   865	                    hardlink_scanner,
   866	                    |tracker, scanner| rename_file_fallback(from, to, Some(tracker), Some(scanner)),
   867	                )
   868	            }

   926	fn rename_dir_fallback(
   927	    from: &Path,
   928	    to: &Path,
   929	    multi_progress: Option<&MultiProgress>,
   930	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_tracker: Option<&mut HardlinkTracker>,
   931	    #[cfg(unix)] hardlink_scanner: Option<&HardlinkGroupScanner>,
   932	) -> io::Result<()> {
   933	    // We remove the destination directory if it exists to match the
   934	    // behavior of `fs::rename`. As far as I can tell, `fs_extra`'s
   935	    // `move_dir` would otherwise behave differently.
   936	    if to.exists() {
   937	        fs::remove_dir_all(to)?;
   938	    }
   939	
   940	    // Calculate total size of directory
   941	    // Silently degrades:
   942	    //    If finding the total size fails for whatever reason,
   943	    //    the progress bar wont be shown for this file / dir.
   944	    //    (Move will probably fail due to permission error later?)
   945	    let total_size = dir_get_size(from).ok();
   946	
   947	    let progress_bar = match (multi_progress, total_size) {
   948	        (Some(multi_progress), Some(total_size)) => {
   949	            let template = "{msg}: [{elapsed_precise}] {wide_bar} {bytes:>7}/{total_bytes:7}";
   950	            let style = ProgressStyle::with_template(template).unwrap();
   951	            let bar = ProgressBar::new(total_size).with_style(style);
   952	            Some(multi_progress.add(bar))
   953	        }
   954	        (_, _) => None,
   955	    };
   956	
   957	    #[cfg(all(unix, not(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "redox"))))]
   958	    let xattrs = fsxattr::retrieve_xattrs(from).unwrap_or_else(|_| HashMap::new());
   959	
   960	    // Use directory copying (with or without hardlink support)
   961	    let result = copy_dir_contents(
   962	        from,
   963	        to,
   964	        #[cfg(unix)]
   965	        hardlink_tracker,
   966	        #[cfg(unix)]
   967	        hardlink_scanner,
   968	        progress_bar.as_ref(),
   969	    );
   970	
   971	    #[cfg(all(unix, not(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "redox"))))]
   972	    fsxattr::apply_xattrs(to, xattrs)?;
   973	
   974	    result?;
   975	
   976	    // Remove the source directory after successful copy
   977	    fs::remove_dir_all(from)?;
   978	
   979	    Ok(())
   980	}

So the kernel's `rename` syscall fails with ENOTDIR when trying to rename a real directory to a symlink (even if the symlink points to a directory). This is because `rename` for directories requires the target to be an actual directory (or not exist), not a symlink.

So with my `rename()` fix alone (without the `handle_two_paths` change), `mv -T real_dir symlink_to_dir` would:
1. Go to `rename()`
2. Pre-check: `to.exists() && to.is_dir() && !to.is_symlink()` → `true && true && false` → skip
3. `fs::rename` fails with ENOTDIR ("Not a directory")

But GNU says "cannot overwrite non-directory with directory" for this case. Our error message would be "Not a directory" which is not as clear. However, this is a pre-existing issue - before my fix, it would also fail (with "Directory not empty" if the target directory is non-empty, or succeed if empty). Actually, before my fix:
- `target_is_dir` = true
- `source_is_dir()` = true
- Goes to `rename()`
- Pre-check: `to.exists() && to.is_dir()` → true (since `to.is_symlink()` check wasn't there)
- `from.is_dir()` → true
- `is_empty_dir(to)` → checks if the directory pointed to by the symlink is empty
- If non-empty: "Directory not empty" error
- If empty: remove the directory pointed to by symlink, then `fs::rename` would try to rename dirA to linkB, which fails with ENOTDIR because linkB is still a symlink (the directory it pointed to was removed, but the symlink itself remains).

So my fix actually improves this case too: instead of incorrectly removing the target directory (or failing with "Directory not empty"), we now skip the pre-check and let the kernel give the appropriate error (ENOTDIR). 

But the `handle_two_paths` change would make this even better: it would go to the else branch (since `target_is_dir` is false when target is a symlink and `-T` is used), and then to `rename()`, which would still fail with ENOTDIR. Actually, same result.

Let me check what my current code does for this case:

With my changes, it still fails (as expected, since the kernel doesn't allow it), but with a less clear error message than GNU's "cannot overwrite non-directory with directory". However, this is the same behavior as before my changes (just a different error path). And this case is not mentioned in the PR description.

Let me also think about whether my `handle_two_paths` change could break anything else. The change is:

```rust
let target_is_symlink = target.is_symlink();
let target_is_dir = target.is_dir()
    && !(opts.no_target_dir && target_is_symlink);
```

This only affects the `-T` case where the target is a symlink. Without `-T`, `target_is_dir` is unchanged. With `-T` and a symlink target, `target_is_dir` becomes false (treating the target as a non-directory), which means:
1. It won't go into the `if target_is_dir` branch (which would call `move_files_into_dir` without `-T` or `rename` with `-T`).
2. It goes to `else if target.exists() && source_is_dir && !(opts.no_target_dir && target_is_symlink)` → now the condition has `!(opts.no_target_dir && target_is_symlink)` which is `!(true && true)` = false, so it goes to the else branch (calling `rename`).
3. In `rename`, the pre-check is skipped because `to.is_symlink()` is true.

This seems correct for all cases:
- `mv -T file symlink_to_dir`: goes to `rename`, replaces symlink with file. ✓
- `mv -T symlink_to_dir symlink_to_dir`: goes to `rename`, replaces symlink with symlink. ✓
- `mv -T dir symlink_to_dir`: goes to `rename`, kernel fails with ENOTDIR (same as before). 
- `mv -T symlink_to_dir dir`: `target_is_dir` = true (real dir), `source_is_dir` = true (symlink to dir). Goes to `rename`, pre-check: `to.exists() && to.is_dir() && !to.is_symlink()` → true (real dir), `from.is_dir()` → true. Checks if directory is empty... if not empty, "Directory not empty". If empty, removes dir and renames. But wait, `fs::rename` would try to rename the symlink to the directory path, which should work.

GNU says "cannot overwrite directory with non-directory". It treats the source symlink as a non-directory (because it's a symlink, not a real directory). Our code treats it as a directory (because `source.is_dir()` follows symlinks).

But should I fix this too? The PR description doesn't mention this case. However, it's related. Let me think about what the correct fix would be:

GNU's logic seems to be:
- When comparing source and target types, use `lstat` (symlink_metadata) not `stat` (metadata).
- If source is a symlink (even to a directory), it's treated as a non-directory.
- If target is a symlink (even to a directory), with `-T`, it's treated as a non-directory.

Our code currently uses `is_dir()` which follows symlinks. To fully match GNU's behavior, we'd need to change how `source_is_dir` is computed:
- Source should be considered a directory only if it's actually a directory (not a symlink to one) OR if it's a symlink to a directory and the target is also a directory (without `-T`).

But this is getting complicated and might be beyond the scope of the PR. The PR specifically says:

> both /run/… paths are symbolic links to directories

And the error is "Directory not empty". My fix addresses this exact scenario.

Let me check if there's a simpler approach: maybe I should also fix the case where source is a symlink to a directory and target is a real directory. The fix would be to check `source.is_symlink()` in the `handle_two_paths` function.

But actually, looking at this case more carefully: what should happen when `mv -T symlink_to_dir real_nonempty_dir`? GNU says "cannot overwrite directory with non-directory" - it refuses because you can't overwrite a directory with a non-directory (and symlink is considered non-directory). The kernel's `rename` would actually fail too: `rename("symlink", "dir")` where dir is a non-empty directory would fail with ENOTEMPTY. So both fail, just with different messages.

I'll leave this as is for now, since it's not the reported issue.

But this would only happen if there's already a file/directory with the same name in the target directory. In that case, the pre-check's behavior is correct: if it's a real non-empty directory, fail; if it's an empty directory, remove and replace; if it's a symlink, skip the check and let `fs::rename` handle it.

My fix correctly skips the pre-check for symlinks in all cases.

- `to.exists()` returns `false` for broken symlinks
- So the pre-check is skipped anyway

And what if `to` is a symlink to a file?
- `to.is_dir()` returns `false`
- Pre-check skipped

cat > /tmp/test_final_comprehensive.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
set -e

PASS_COUNT=0
FAIL_COUNT=0

run_test() {
    local test_name="$1"
    local expected_result="$2"  # "pass" or "fail"
    shift 2
    
    echo "=== $test_name ==="
    "$@" 2>&1
    local exit_code=$?
    
    if [ "$expected_result" = "pass" ] && [ $exit_code -eq 0 ]; then
        echo "✓ PASS"
        ((PASS_COUNT++))
    elif [ "$expected_result" = "fail" ] && [ $exit_code -ne 0 ]; then
        echo "✓ PASS (expected failure)"
        ((PASS_COUNT++))
    else
        echo "✗ FAIL (expected $expected_result, got exit code $exit_code)"
        ((FAIL_COUNT++))
    fi
    echo ""
}

MV="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils mv"

# Test 1: Both symlinks to dirs, with -T (the main PR issue)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB
run_test "Test 1: mv -T symlink_to_dir symlink_to_dir" "pass" \
    $MV -T linkA linkB
[ "$(readlink linkB)" = "dirA" ] && echo "  -> linkB correctly points to dirA" || { echo "  -> FAIL: linkB points to $(readlink linkB)"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
[ ! -e linkA ] && echo "  -> linkA correctly removed" || { echo "  -> FAIL: linkA still exists"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 2: Both symlinks to dirs, without -T (should move into target)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB
run_test "Test 2: mv symlink_to_dir symlink_to_dir (no -T)" "pass" \
    $MV linkA linkB
[ -L "dirB/linkA" ] && echo "  -> linkA moved into dirB" || { echo "  -> FAIL"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 3: Real dir to real empty dir, with -T (should succeed)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
run_test "Test 3: mv -T real_dir real_empty_dir" "pass" \
    $MV -T dirA dirB
[ ! -e dirA ] && [ -d dirB ] && echo "  -> dirA renamed to dirB" || { echo "  -> FAIL"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 4: Real dir to real non-empty dir, with -T (should fail)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
run_test "Test 4: mv -T real_dir real_nonempty_dir" "fail" \
    $MV -T dirA dirB
[ -d dirA ] && [ -d dirB ] && echo "  -> both dirs still exist (correct)" || { echo "  -> FAIL"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 5: Regular file to symlink-to-dir, with -T (should replace symlink)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirB linkB
echo "hello" > regular_file
run_test "Test 5: mv -T file symlink_to_dir" "pass" \
    $MV -T regular_file linkB
[ -f linkB ] && [ ! -L linkB ] && echo "  -> symlink replaced by regular file" || { echo "  -> FAIL"; ((FAIL_COUNT++)); }
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

# Test 6: Symlink-to-dir to regular file, with -T (should fail with appropriate error)
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA
ln -s dirA linkA
echo "hello" > regular_file
run_test "Test 6: mv -T symlink_to_dir file" "fail" \
    $MV -T linkA regular_file
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

echo "=========================================="
echo "Results: $PASS_COUNT passed, $FAIL_COUNT failed"
EOF

#!/bin/bash

MV="/testbed/target/debug/coreutils mv"

cd "$TESTDIR"

touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirA linkA
ln -s dirB linkB
$MV -T linkA linkB
echo "Exit: $?"
echo "linkB -> $(readlink linkB)"

TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirB
touch dirB/somefile
ln -s dirB linkB
echo "hello" > regular_file
$MV -T regular_file linkB
echo "Exit: $?"
[ -f linkB ] && [ ! -L linkB ] && echo "PASS: symlink replaced by regular file" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

echo ""
echo "=== Test 3: mv -T real_dir real_nonempty_dir ==="
TESTDIR=$(mktemp -d)
cd "$TESTDIR"
mkdir -p dirA dirB
touch dirB/somefile
$MV -T dirA dirB
echo "Exit: $?"
[ -d dirA ] && [ -d dirB ] && echo "PASS: both still exist" || echo "FAIL"
rm -rf "$TESTDIR"

echo ""
echo "All tests done."
EOF

   380	    // behavior: `mv -T file symlink_to_dir` replaces the symlink, not the directory it points to.

   753	
   754	    // "to" may no longer exist if it was backed up
   755	    // If 'to' is a symlink, we should not check if it's an empty directory;
   756	    // the underlying rename syscall will replace the symlink itself,
   757	    // not the directory it points to.
   758	    if to.exists() && to.is_dir() && !to.is_symlink() {
   759	        // normalize behavior between *nix and windows
   760	        if from.is_dir() {
   761	            if is_empty_dir(to) {
   762	                fs::remove_dir(to)?;
   763	            } else {
   764	                return Err(io::Error::other(translate!("mv-error-directory-not-empty")));
   765	            }
   766	        }

My changes look correct. Let me summarize what I changed:

1. **In `handle_two_paths` function (line 378-384):** Added a check for when `--no-target-directory` (-T) is used and the target is a symlink. In that case, the target should be treated as a non-directory (the symlink itself should be replaced, not the directory it points to). This matches GNU `mv` behavior.

2. **In `handle_two_paths` function (line 423):** Extended the condition for the "non-directory to directory" error to also exclude the case where `-T` is used and target is a symlink. This prevents false errors when replacing a symlink with a directory.

3. **In `rename` function (line 758):** Added `!to.is_symlink()` to the pre-check condition. When the target is a symlink, we should not check if the directory it points to is empty, because the `rename` syscall will replace the symlink itself, not follow it.

These changes fix the issue described in the PR: moving a directory symlink to another directory symlink now works correctly (replaces the symlink instead of checking the contents of the directory it points to).
